  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_00d52e47-4664-4745-858d-3bb4fd5a1bb2'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText4346021532003266222" style="display:none">This National Book Award Finalist is now a major motion picture -- one of the most buzzed-about films at Sundance 2013, starring Shailene Woodley and Miles Teller.<br /><br />SUTTER KEELY. HE’S the guy you want at your party. He’ll get everyone dancing. He’ ll get everyone in your parents’ pool. Okay, so he’s not exactly a shining academic star. He has no plans for college and will probably end up folding men’s shirts for a living. But there are plenty of ladies in town, and with the help of Dean Martin and Seagram’s V.O., life’s pretty fabuloso, actually.<br /><br />Until the morning he wakes up on a random front lawn, and he meets Aimee. Aimee’s clueless. Aimee is a social disaster. Aimee needs help, and it’s up to the Sutterman to show Aimee a splendiferous time and then let her go forth and prosper. But Aimee’s not like other girls, and before long he’s in way over his head. For the first time in his life, he has the power to make a difference in someone else’s life—or ruin it forever.</span>

<a href="/questions/120186-what-did-you-think-of-the-ending-did">What did you think of the ending? Did Sutter do the right thing?</a>
</div>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_120186'><a id="like_count_community_question_120186" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/120186?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F3798703-the-spectacular-now">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/51076846-bookishbabe-jpg"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1451968888i/51076846._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/51076846-bookishbabe-jpg">Bookishbabe.Jpg</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I loved the ending of this book. It was realistic and honest. Sometimes people learn life lessons slowly. <br /><br /><br />we already see that Sutter is heading down t<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I loved the ending of this book. It was realistic and honest. Sometimes people learn life lessons slowly. <br /><br /><br />we already see that Sutter is heading down the road of being an alcoholic and following his fathers footsteps. In the beginning he was selfish but has a huge heart to and tries to do the right thing. When he was driving the little boy back to his house when he was running away, even though he was doing something good he was also drinking while driving. It shows you his priorities. At the end when he let Aimee go he was being selfless because he knows he wasn't the one for her. I do agree he could of been honest in the first place. . In my mind I'd like to think this isn't the end of their story. Sutter still has a lot to learn he is only 18.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<a href="/questions/390729-is-it-necessary-to-read-the-book-before">Is it necessary to read the book before watching the film?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_390729'><a id="like_count_community_question_390729" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/390729?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F3798703-the-spectacular-now">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/405544-blythe"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442959420i/405544._UY100_CR24,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/405544-blythe">Blythe</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It is not at all necessary to read the book first. Both the book and film have good things going for them; the book gives more insight into Sutter, bu<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It is not at all necessary to read the book first. Both the book and film have good things going for them; the book gives more insight into Sutter, but the film does a far better job of making Aimee a real full-fledged person. In the book she's rather flat. I saw the movie first and then read the book, and enjoyed that order.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_289523456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/289523456" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289523456?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375865022" href="/book/show/7961827-the-spectacular-now">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289523456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9804246990968877660">On finishing The Spectacular Now I feel hollowed out and slightly sick – not because the ending was bad but because as much as I didn’t want it to, it ended in probably the most realistic way it could. <br/><br/>Part of me wants to gouge whatever scraps of hope I can from the close of Sutter’s story, hold onto the hints that things can and will eventually change, because not doing that hurts so much. I want to pretend that last chapter doesn’t exist, but in way, it’s that last chapter that makes this book</span>
  <span id="freeText9804246990968877660" style="display:none">On finishing The Spectacular Now I feel hollowed out and slightly sick – not because the ending was bad but because as much as I didn’t want it to, it ended in probably the most realistic way it could. <br /><br />Part of me wants to gouge whatever scraps of hope I can from the close of Sutter’s story, hold onto the hints that things can and will eventually change, because not doing that hurts so much. I want to pretend that last chapter doesn’t exist, but in way, it’s that last chapter that makes this book what it is. It’s that ending that makes me acknowledge what I don’t want to see; this is the real world and sometimes things are devastating and not everyone gets a happy ending. There’s no emotional montage, there’s no countdown to the big romantic climax – there’s some tie off, but the ends are left bloody and uncauterised. <br /><br />That, I believe, is what prevents this from being another “issues” book, another dire warning on how bad choices can screw up a life. I think this book trusts the reader to drawn their own conclusions. And because of that, I think it’s a more realistic portrayal of addiction – it’s not a black and white story. We see the patterns of desctruction and the harm Sutter causes to himself and those around him, but we also see the charisma, the charm and the highs that perpetuate the cycle. It’s sympathy and abhorrence all wound up in a complicated tangle of being able to relate and yet being a helpless oberserver as events escalate toward the conclusion. <br /><br />I can’t state enough how the relationship between Sutter and Aimee tore at me. Tharp wrote this part of the story so powerfully; I felt anxious and helpless as I read, knowing where it was going and wanting to close my eyes to it, yet knowing there was no other way it could go. <br /><br />There were so many scenes in between them – Aimee’s vulnerability and complete lack of guile, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sutter telling her to shut up, Aimee’s confession of what happened to her when she was 14, Sutter’s eventual cognizance of what he will do to her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - just tore me up inside. I absolutely believed these two people, and how they interacted. Sutter’s actions - whether selfish, compassionate or simply misguided -felt authentic. That he would carry out his final decision in the manner he chose too was awful but ultimately understandable – I believed that he would do that and that he would feel it was the best way he could do it. <br /><br />Tharp’s subtley in portraying Sutter’s downslide was handled well. He keeps us firmly in Sutter’s point of view, but allows us glimpses of the altering perspectives around him, the way others begin to perceive his behaviour. These voices, on the fringes of Sutter’s awareness, balance out his wilful blindness. We’re made aware of his own downward trajectory by the changes in the people who surround him, or who used to surround him. Tharp manages to convey the seriousness of what’s going on without slipping out of Sutter’s voice, and without beating the reader over the head with heavy messaging. <br /><br />The weakest part of this story for me was the plotline with Sutter’s father. I feel like this was truncated in order to fit within the confines of the novel, and not strictly realistic in terms of how quickly and fully Sutter’s moment of realisation hit. It’s a minor quibble though, it’s not the circumstances I don’t buy, but rather now they are neatly shoehorned into the climax of the book. <br /><br />If I put aside my hurt, raw feelings about the ending of this book – I can be objective and realise that it’s brilliant. Sutter is an accessible and compelling narrator – even while being appalled at his actions it’s easy to remain engaged by him, taken in by his easy charm. It’s the kind of writing that sinks its hooks in without realising that it’s happening. You get caught up in the rhythm of Sutter’s voice and the warp of his perspective. So much so that even while I suspected all along this book and I were not going to ride off into a sunset of happiness, I still felt sucker punched at the end. <br /><br />So perhaps the most powerful thing about this book is not just it’s unapologetic honesty, but that when it delivers it’s final blow, it’s not the one you’re expecting. But it’s the one that’s the most real. So it hurts the worst. <br /><br />* * * * * <br />Oh shit, that ending. I feel like someone has dug out my insides with a blunt spoon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9804246990968877660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_204594326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204594326" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204594326?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204594326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10450162144039701436"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Okay... so I've been putting off this review because I was unsure about my rating. My initial reaction was <b>FIVE STARS!! FIVE STARS!!</b> but then I got to thinking about my dislike for the ending and thought maybe I should round it down to four... and then I was like "but is my problem with the ending because it was bad - or because it didn't go the way I wanted it to?"... so I eventually kept my five stars because I am so completely in love with the amazingly complicated and wonderful character</span>
  <span id="freeText10450162144039701436" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Okay... so I've been putting off this review because I was unsure about my rating. My initial reaction was <b>FIVE STARS!! FIVE STARS!!</b> but then I got to thinking about my dislike for the ending and thought maybe I should round it down to four... and then I was like "but is my problem with the ending because it was bad - or because it didn't go the way I wanted it to?"... so I eventually kept my five stars because I am so completely in love with the amazingly complicated and wonderful character that is Sutter Keely. He is complex, multi-dimensional, so vibrant and full of life that it's hard to accept that he isn't real and about to jump off the page.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/321382.Tim_Tharp" title="Tim Tharp" rel="nofollow noopener">Tim Tharp</a> has written a very funny, sad, thoughtful book that creates such an in-depth picture of a boy who is simultaneously lovable and exhausting. I am friends with the female equivalent of Sutter Keely, a person who you always want at your parties because you know they'll bring every social situation to life, a person who is kind and means well but is very hard to deal with in any more than small doses, a person who is nearly always just a little drunk. How many times have I rolled my eyes and thought "okay, give it a rest now"? I think I can appreciate the world through their eyes a little bit more after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3798703.The_Spectacular_Now" title="The Spectacular Now by Tim Tharp" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spectacular Now</a>.<br><br>Sutter is the kind of multi-layered character I love to read about. On the surface he's a warm-hearted, over-the-top drunk, the kind of guy who's popular in high school but will probably never end up achieving his potential because his aspirations don't extend further than locating his next alcohol fix. Underneath all this he is troubled and sad and lonely, people often think that a drinker's problem is the alcohol, but nine times out of ten it runs far deeper than this. His dad is nowhere to be seen, his mum and stepdad seem to have forgotten he exists except for when they pause to threaten him with military school, his best friend no longer wants to hang around with him, he's just been dumped... and then along comes Aimee. The one person in the world who has ever seemed to need him, truly need him, to get her life back in order, to gain confidence and to sort out her future. Can Sutter finally make a difference beyond the small realm of his booze-fuelled spectacular now?<br><br>I'm still not sure how I feel about that ending. Do I like the fact that this book doesn't carry the message that we were all hoping for and expecting? Not really. But is this a representation of real life in all its fucked up, messy, sad, sometimes funny glory? Probably... yeah, probably. I guess in real life not everyone gets saved and perhaps that was what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/321382.Tim_Tharp" title="Tim Tharp" rel="nofollow noopener">Tim Tharp</a> was trying to say.</span>

<div id="review_182550641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182550641" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182550641?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423399636" href="/book/show/7961828-spectacular-now-the">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2507910-peep-pop-pop">Peep (Pop! Pop!)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182550641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13655043618069497206">I’m not sure if this book would have affected me quite as much if I didn’t know this boy. He is one of the people that I love the most on this planet, and he shares more DNA with me than anyone else. He’s intelligent, effortlessly popular, charming, kind, and entertaining. He has a big heart, fragile and exposed. We once spent hours in our backyard collecting slugs and setting them up in their very own tree stump castle. Once when he was facing a spanking, we schemed and plotted, arming ourselve</span>
  <span id="freeText13655043618069497206" style="display:none">I’m not sure if this book would have affected me quite as much if I didn’t know this boy. He is one of the people that I love the most on this planet, and he shares more DNA with me than anyone else. He’s intelligent, effortlessly popular, charming, kind, and entertaining. He has a big heart, fragile and exposed. We once spent hours in our backyard collecting slugs and setting them up in their very own tree stump castle. Once when he was facing a spanking, we schemed and plotted, arming ourselves with sticks for weapons. We were thick as thieves. But we all deal with the stress and trauma of childhood in different ways; we all have our coping mechanisms. As we grew up we fumbled our way down different roads, which led us further and further apart. I learned how to live inside my own skin, fired to hardness like pottery. He learned to smother everything under a chemically induced happiness.<br /><br />I think that’s the most heartbreaking thing about Sutter Keely – he’s smothering himself. I can so easily feel the pain seeping out of the cracks in his bonhomie: when he reflects on all the girls that like him, but never seem to love him; when he thinks about how much better off his father is, now that he’s no longer living with his mother; when he tells the mother of a lost child, “Your son is hurting. He misses his Dad.” He can so clearly see the pain of others, but he can’t see his own grief, disappointment, and heartbreak at all. He’s the shoulder everyone likes to cry on, and he can’t see a friend in pain without trying to fix it, but he has no ability to fix himself.<br /><br />I think that this is one of the most accurate portrayals of addiction that I’ve read. So many books tend to gloss over it, or go in the other direction and become “issue” books, and completely forget that addicts are still <i>people</i>. This book captures so much of the essence of addiction, and the first person narration lets us in on all of the bullshit he feeds himself to cope with the loneliness and self-hatred.<br /><br />I know that the ending seems dark, but I found a bit of hope in this story. Aimee and Sutter are two lost kids, and while there are moments of honesty and beauty in their relationship, they cannot build anything solid when they are both dealing (or not dealing) with so many internal battles. Sutter’s method of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ending things <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> seems incredibly realistic to me: both selfless and selfish at the same time, and suffused with his heartbreaking lack of self-worth. I’d like to find hope in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sutter’s increasing lows. Pain like that can’t be contained forever, and I do feel that despite the ending, he has begun to see certain things more clearly. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That may be just because I’d like to hope that my brother can get better someday, though.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Bright Eyes – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CqlsVypKIu8" rel="nofollow noopener">Landlocked Blues</a><br /><br />So many parts of this song remind me of this book: the questionable security of the future, isolation, the liquid cure, the “one quotable phrase, ‘if you love something give it away.’”<br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/04/post-title-click-and-type-to-edit2.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13655043618069497206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_614370441" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614370441" />
    <a title="K-L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13365703-k-l"><img alt="K-L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587318826p2/13365703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614370441?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K-L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K-L" href="/user/show/13365703-k-l">K-L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13365703-k-l?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13365703-k-l?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13365703-k-l?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13365703-k-l?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614370441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6015178524241091328">"Life is a big, screwed-up joke with its ups and downs. The best way to deal with it is to live in the now, pursue all the pleasure and deal with none of the grief." <br/><br/>That's the message I get from Sutter Keely, protagonist of <i>The Spectacular Now</i>. He takes a purely hedonistic, somewhat philosophical world view throughout the book. Tharp gives Sutton a clear, blunt, narrative voice but when it comes to character development, Sutter stays the same person from point A to point B, even with inserting </span>
  <span id="freeText6015178524241091328" style="display:none">"Life is a big, screwed-up joke with its ups and downs. The best way to deal with it is to live in the now, pursue all the pleasure and deal with none of the grief." <br /><br />That's the message I get from Sutter Keely, protagonist of <i>The Spectacular Now</i>. He takes a purely hedonistic, somewhat philosophical world view throughout the book. Tharp gives Sutton a clear, blunt, narrative voice but when it comes to character development, Sutter stays the same person from point A to point B, even with inserting numerous potential turning points for him.<br /><br />Sutter defines himself as "God's own drunk". And drinking does seem to be his life's philosophy; he barely gets through any encounter in the book without a flask or 7UP/whiskey in hand. He doesn't confront his own problems, despite supposedly 'helping' new love Aimee come out of her shell. He's ultimately a likeable character, but as I read on, he became like a guest who has overstayed his welcome.<br /><br />As for the plot, where did it go? The plot could easily just have been a set of serial anecdotes. There are too many loose ends, no closure. You're left with too many questions, and no answers--and not in a good way. Maybe that's how Tharp intended for it to go, a story that pantomimes real life for pleasure-seekers. Real life doesn't have closure; sometimes we end up shelving our problems in the back of our drunk brains as life goes on.<br /><br />I guess that's ultimately the true message of the novel, hopeless as it is. Sutton had a drinking problem, family issues, a skewed view of life, but in the end, he brushes everything aside and lives in the "Spectacular Now". <br /><br />Conclusions? Well-written, funny, but half-hearted in terms of plot and character development. Instead of a real story, we get a portrait of a hedonistic, broken yet charismatic boy who approaches life with a swagger in his step, a joke in his eyes, and a flask in his hand.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6015178524241091328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_817884549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/817884549" />
    <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden"><img alt="Katrina Passick Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959676p2/1964146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/817884549?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer817884549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10482838336571404835">Holy crap, this is a good book. <br/><br/>A <i>heavy</i> book. This is one of those books that I went into thinking it was going to be a romance with a message, but pretty all-around feel-good. <br/><br/>No. Nope. I mean, yeah, there's a message, all right, but this book isn't exactly a fluffy candy feel-good story. So don't go into it thinking it will be. It's funny and philosophical and introspective and reminiscent. Sutter's voice is so authentically teenager that it's obvious Tim Tharp never completely forgot that pha</span>
  <span id="freeText10482838336571404835" style="display:none">Holy crap, this is a good book. <br /><br />A <i>heavy</i> book. This is one of those books that I went into thinking it was going to be a romance with a message, but pretty all-around feel-good. <br /><br />No. Nope. I mean, yeah, there's a message, all right, but this book isn't exactly a fluffy candy feel-good story. So don't go into it thinking it will be. It's funny and philosophical and introspective and reminiscent. Sutter's voice is so authentically teenager that it's obvious Tim Tharp never completely forgot that phase in his own life. Some of us do remember what it was like to be a teenager. How much is sucked at times, but also how amazingly high you could feel even when everything around you was total shit. <br /><br />It's really hard to encapsulate all the things going through my head after reading a book like this. I <i>just</i> finished it, so while the story and all its intricacies are still fresh, it's also...well, still fresh. It messes with my ability to put everything in words. So I suppose I'll let Tharp's words do it for me:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"It's superb to be out in the early, early morning before the sun comes up. There's this sense of being super-alive. You're in on a secret that all the dull, sleeping people don't know about. Unlike them, you're alert and aware of existing right here in this precise moment between what happened and what's going to happen."<br /><br />"The whole magnetic thing about sex is you want the other person to want <i>you</i>. I mean, that's what separates us from the animals. That and haircuts."<br /><br />"Besides, it doesn't matter if it's real. It never does with dreams. They aren't anything anyway but lifesavers to cling to so you don't drown. Life is an ocean, and most everyone's holding on to some kind of dream to keep afloat."</b>
</i><br /><br />I applaud Mr. Tharp on his realistic, unbiased portrayal of teenagers. His characters have sex, drink, and do drugs, but he never crosses the line into moralizing or overdramatizing. The kids aren't getting so wasted they rape each other or set cars on fire or have dumpster babies, but neither are they preaching about how wrong it is or having serious internal debates about whether or not they should have sex. Things just <i>are</i>, and that's missing in a lot of literature. I've noticed the "to sex or not to sex" dilemma pops up in a <i>lot</i> of YA fiction written by women, and I think it's a subject that really needs to be treated a little more fairly. People seem to think that sex is the end-all, be-all of teenage stories, when really, being a teenager is about a lot more than hormones. Sometimes, your teenage son or daughter having sex isn't the thing you should be worrying about most.<br /><br />I couldn't get over Sutter. Kid breaks my heart every time I think of him. So much love to give, so much potential for emotional greatness, an untapped inner prosperity that some of us only dream of having. He's such a cynic at heart, but tries so hard to be optimistic, and then his optimism shines through in such a twisted, almost nihilistic way. He can't plan for the future because he has no hope, but he can't come to grips with that. He's one of those guys that's in denial all the time. He's not depressed because, hey, what does he have to be depressed about? He's not an alcoholic because, hey, he can quit any time he wants to. He's not in love with anyone because, hey, what <i>is</i> love, anyway? On the surface he seems really superficial, but as you get to know him, you see the kid's got a heart bigger than most and, sadly, it's been beaten to a bloody pulp and I'm not sure if there's much anyone can do about it. <br /><br />Like I said, it's heavy. But a really, really good heavy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10482838336571404835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1654454916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30863291-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527983001p2/30863291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1654454916?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/30863291-philip">Philip</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=movie-is-better">movie-is-better</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1654454916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6024646625580230043">4.5 ish stars. <br/><br/>Call me an idiot if you like, but I didn't realize this book existed until a week ago. I ended up seeing the theatrical adaptation at a free screening when it first came out in 2013 not really knowing what I was getting myself into (except, of course, a movie theater- for free) but the movie affected me and I fell in love with it because it immediately connected to my experience as a young adult without resorting to terminal illnesses or similar plot devices to get me invested int</span>
  <span id="freeText6024646625580230043" style="display:none">4.5 ish stars. <br /><br />Call me an idiot if you like, but I didn't realize this book existed until a week ago. I ended up seeing the theatrical adaptation at a free screening when it first came out in 2013 not really knowing what I was getting myself into (except, of course, a movie theater- for free) but the movie affected me and I fell in love with it because it immediately connected to my experience as a young adult without resorting to terminal illnesses or similar plot devices to get me invested into the lives of the characters. It's embarrassing for me to admit that I chalked it up to the screenwriters as being the brilliant masterminds behind the story, when really it's Tim Tharp who gave them the prime material to work with. It wasn't until good ol' Goodreads suggested the book to me that I realized my life had been a lie. I immediately started reading and was affected all over again in the best way.<br /><br />It's kind of hard for me to separate the book from the movie after having seen it and my review would probably be a little different if I were able to differentiate them adequately. For example, my perception of Aimee might be a little different if I hadn't already fallen in love with Shailene Woodley's portrayal of her. Without her filling in the gaps, would I find book Aimee and her relationship with Sutter as believable? I don't know, but I think probably not. Or not as much. <br /><br />And that ending... Would I hate it if I didn't supplement it with the ending of the movie? I mean, I like to tell myself that I respect "realist" endings- ones that don't need to end happy and tie up all loose ends. But deep down I'm a sentimentalist, dang-it! I choose to hold on to hope, just like Aimee, and for that reason, I love this book. Or maybe just the book/movie hybrid. There's no way to know anymore....</span>
  <a data-text-id="6024646625580230043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_204513384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204513384" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369004887p2/2753251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204513384?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375865022" href="/book/show/7961827-the-spectacular-now">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of The Catcher in the Rye.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alyssa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=a-guy-of-ya">a-guy-of-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=get-with-library">get-with-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=reccomended">reccomended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=i-love-this-cover">i-love-this-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=great-realistic-fiction">great-realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=great-books">great-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204513384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7663683448708761712">Life’s a party for Sutter Keely because <i>he’s</i> the life of the party. He’s the guy who has friends from every social circle, can get people laughing in awkward situations, and has a smile every time you see him. He’s the definition of “happy drunk,” and since he’s drunk <i>all the time</i>, he’s just a happy guy all around. He lets nothing get him down, not even when his “beautiful fat girlfriend” Cassidy dumps him or when Ricky, his best friend, starts to follow the clean route. Nope, nothing, not even </span>
  <span id="freeText7663683448708761712" style="display:none">Life’s a party for Sutter Keely because <i>he’s</i> the life of the party. He’s the guy who has friends from every social circle, can get people laughing in awkward situations, and has a smile every time you see him. He’s the definition of “happy drunk,” and since he’s drunk <i>all the time</i>, he’s just a happy guy all around. He lets nothing get him down, not even when his “beautiful fat girlfriend” Cassidy dumps him or when Ricky, his best friend, starts to follow the clean route. Nope, nothing, not even the absence of his father or the fakeness of his female relatives, can get Sutter down, because there’s always another drink for ‘God’s own drunk.’<br /><br />Everyone knows a guy like Sutter Keely. I happen to know three or four. He’s the guy who’s so sweet, so kind and warm-hearted, the type who you could see turning out to be something big but will never get anywhere because he thinks he’s bound to head down the downward spiral. He’s the guy who looks shallow on the outside but is really intellectual and <i>spectacular</i> on the inside. He’s the guy who’s in the absence of dreams and heroes and has to go looking to something else to abandon that emptiness. I loved Sutter, this broken, broken boy. He had the biggest heart, and his intentions were always in the right place, even if he made bad decisions and things didn’t always turn out like he planned. I think Tharp reflected alcoholism realistically and suitably on Sutter, even if sometimes it was hard for me, loving Sutter and all, to handle a 7UP and whiskey nearly every scene.<br /><br />Sutter starts out a drunk in the beginning of the book, and not many changes happen with him as we go along. Sutter was the person who could change others but couldn’t change himself – this guy who thinks he’s incapable of being loved <i>loves</i> others so well because he won’t let others fall to pieces. I think such is why this book isn’t as depressing as it could have turned out – there’s hope and there’s the fact that addiction doesn’t identify a person. Cassidy, after Sutter, would have had to be my favourite character. Not only did Tharp give her a personality - ex-girlfriend's are real people, you know - but he gave her rendition and space to show why Sutter loved her in the first place. A lot of the time, you'll read about an ex-girlfriend that's a complete bitch, and you wonder how the main character could love that. Cassidy, even if not a huge character, sort of made the book for me, as did Ricky, the multi-dimensional best friend who was exactly perfect and nothing like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96453231" rel="nofollow noopener">other best friends who have all the potential but never make anything of it.</a><br /><br />Tharp presented the life of teens as well as he did alcoholism. Where I go to school, sure, there are social circles and the “popular” kids, but everyone hangs out with everyone. Life isn’t always the geek-VS-jock bullshit we’re always reading about and Tharp reflected that aspect perfectly. I think he chose a risky subject to write about – taking a look at other reviews, people seem to think he went overboard – but that he did it justice. I wouldn’t recommend this book to everyone, honestly – it’s a hard book to read, it tackles subjects that not all people are comfortable reading about, and you have to dig deep to find the layered message – but it’s a book that can really impact a person if they take the time to read it through. <br /><br />The first two sentences might be complete turn-offs – <i>“So, it’s a little before ten a.m. and I’m just starting to get a good buzz on. Theoretically, I should be in Algebra II, but in reality I’m cruising over to my beautiful fat girlfriend Cassidy’s house.”</i> – but whatever you do, don’t stop reading. This likely won’t be a story you’ll soon forget.<br /><br />THE SPECTACULAR NOW by Tim Tharp<br />Audience: 14+ (questionable content, questionable language, sexual occurrences, drug abuse, alcohol abuse)<br />Rating: 5/5<br />Recommend?: I wish for you to read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7663683448708761712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9071517383158851009">Here we go..<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358188i/709377.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It would have been a 5stars book except for Aimee (I couldn't figure her out and she was a bit too naive for my taste; all that planning scared me to be honest.. and not telling anyone her secret? oh boy, that's just wrong) and the ending (which I still don't get, not really.. I might need to re-read the last page). Can I also have one more page please? <br/><br/>So.. a full review might follow - if I'll have some down time to write it *sigh* - but 'til then this is what I liked:<br/><br/>- Sutter - wit</span>
  <span id="freeText9071517383158851009" style="display:none">Here we go..<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358188i/709377.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It would have been a 5stars book except for Aimee (I couldn't figure her out and she was a bit too naive for my taste; all that planning scared me to be honest.. and not telling anyone her secret? oh boy, that's just wrong) and the ending (which I still don't get, not really.. I might need to re-read the last page). Can I also have one more page please? <br><br>So.. a full review might follow - if I'll have some down time to write it *sigh* - but 'til then this is what I liked:<br><br>- Sutter - with his fun side and the deep side (that he hides behind his remarks and his drinking and him making other people have a good time).<br>- His little chats with his best friend (even though the "best" part is quite doubtable)<br>- His inner thoughts - he might not sound like a real guy, but he had me laughing or thinking about some things he said here an there.. I have tons of quotes that I liked to testify if you won't have my word)<br>- The writing - I just picked this book up and couldn't put it down. I didn't want to. <br>- Also I loved remembering high-school - so many parties, having fun, having no worries, feeling free, forgetting about everything bad and finding ways to enjoy every moment. It's not like we don't do those things now, but we are more quite about it, less free, more down-to-earth .. or it just feels this way.<br>- Aaaaand.. some other things that might spoil the fun for you<br><br>Anyways, I loved this story, the humor, the emotional part.. everything. I thought it was supposed to be a light, funny read (not sure where I got that idea from) but at times it felt pretty heavy.<br><br>And yes, there is swearing and drinking and some talk about sex, I am not sure why people keep warning about hese things in their reviews, where do you live in a bubble so you don't find that in real life? <br>No, no need to explain, I get that you don't like reading about those things (I am getting bothered by other things too that don't seem to bother you one bit) I just had it on the tip of my fingers, so I had to let it out.<br><br>Also I am not sure how you do it (the parenting stuff), but when I was young it only took my parents to not let me do some things and .. challenge accepted! ^_^ <br>If you don't buy a book for them, they will borrow it from their friends and read it without you knowing it.<br>And even though there are drugs and a lot of drinks and driving (while having a drink) in this story, there are many other things that make this book worth reading... and by young people too.<br><br>Back to the point:<br>Loved this book, Tim Tharp I am keeping my eyes on you now!<br><br>PS: Oh.. [the 3rd thing I didn't like that much:] I know that boys don't necessarily like skinny girls, but the "fat girlfriend" thing got old and pretty fast. Yes, I got it the first time around, she was fat and beautiful. <br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><i>"The color flow into your lungs, into your bloodstream. You are the colors"</i>. <br>( ~ Amazon preview )<br><br>How in the world did I forget to order this book? <br>I'm telling you, I'm getting old :)))</span>

<div id="review_130504861" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130504861" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42508-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368721201p2/42508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130504861?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/42508-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=books-for-kids">books-for-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130504861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer141631314618375630">This is a weird book. The book itself is pretty straight-forward, the narrator is a high school senior named Sutter who likes to drink and is the life of the party. The party to him though is all of life. He's always the life of the party even though most people probably don't realize the party is happening. He lives by the motto of 'embrace the weird', meaning just go with whatever happens and make the best of it. Part of his embracing whatever happens is knocking back enough whiskey to make th</span>
  <span id="freeText141631314618375630" style="display:none">This is a weird book. The book itself is pretty straight-forward, the narrator is a high school senior named Sutter who likes to drink and is the life of the party. The party to him though is all of life. He's always the life of the party even though most people probably don't realize the party is happening. He lives by the motto of 'embrace the weird', meaning just go with whatever happens and make the best of it. Part of his embracing whatever happens is knocking back enough whiskey to make the weird palatable and normal. <br /><br />What's weird to me is that this is classified as a teen book. I don't want to come across as priggish or a prude or anything like that, but I usually figured teen books should have some kind of 'good' in them. They should be some kind of mini-little-morality-play. Sutter should realize that his life is going no-where, he should have some moment where he sees that there needs to be more to life than acting like the fun jackass and being drunk all the time. <br /><br />If I substitute the drinking in the book for smoking copious amounts of pot on a daily basis Sutter isn't all that different from quite a few friends and acquaintances of mine in my late high school and college years. Thinking of Sutter as some of my old friends, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GdKZQTfEGCk" rel="nofollow noopener"> this song </a> started to play in my head. The weird innocence of being young and fucked up, something that maybe it's fine to be but which doesn't really last and eventually becomes being a fucked up fuck up. <br /><br />As the book moved on I wanted to see Sutter learn something, and everytime he seemed to learn a lesson he would in no time show the bit of learning he did to be an aberration that was quickly corrected by another reckless action. Even towards the end of the book the progress that the reader sees him make is put into relief by the very last chapter that can be seen as either a stand for youth against the encroachment of early adulthood or as someone who is never really going to learn anything as long as there are people willing to cheer him on for his antics. Which makes me think that instead of the wistful reminiscences of the Wilco song above Sutter's future is more likely going to be more like this darker Uncle Tupelo <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UsuWfo4sx70" rel="nofollow noopener">song</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="141631314618375630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3569121713431722504" style="display:none">Every time I read a book that is popular I almost always end up hating it. What's wrong with me? Or maybe I should as what is wrong with everyone else?! <br><br>I wanted to read this book before I went to go see the movie, but I only want to go see the movie so I can scope out the acting of the two main characters since they are both casted for Divergent. Sorry having your main character being an alcoholic doesn't cut it as main conflict.<br><br>How this book won/was nominated for awards floors me. I can't believe adults even allow their children to read this. If I had teens I would most certainly not allow them to read it. I absolutely hate alcohol, but this book glorifies it. The main character drinks and drinks and glorifies drinking, kids will read this book and be like "wow he's got something going here maybe I should try it." Then he drinks and drives ALL the time. I hate it. <br><br>He talks about not remembering what happened the pervious night he was obviously black out drunk, anyone who knows anything KNOWs that being black out drunk, you can not drive safely. You can't even walk, but this kids some how does it every day with no consequences. Then tenes are reading this book and thinking it's no big deal! It is a big deal!<br><br>just NO! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380433318ra/871928.gif" width="500" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_253670213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253670213" />
    <a title="ALPHAreader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4285990-alphareader"><img alt="ALPHAreader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457410626p2/4285990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253670213?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ALPHAreader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ALPHAreader" href="/user/show/4285990-alphareader">ALPHAreader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4285990-alphareader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253670213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer22331481160965451">Everyone knows that if you want a good time, you call Sutter Keely. He’s the guy with a bar in his boot, enough whisky in his flask to go round and he doesn’t know the meaning of the word ‘embarrassment’. There’s no doubt that Sutter is the life of any party – but when it comes to relationships, he fizzes pretty quick. He’s accumulated a string of ex-girlfriends in his eighteen years, and remained friends with every single one of them. But right now he’s hoping to hold on to his current girlfrie</span>
  <span id="freeText22331481160965451" style="display:none">Everyone knows that if you want a good time, you call Sutter Keely. He’s the guy with a bar in his boot, enough whisky in his flask to go round and he doesn’t know the meaning of the word ‘embarrassment’. There’s no doubt that Sutter is the life of any party – but when it comes to relationships, he fizzes pretty quick. He’s accumulated a string of ex-girlfriends in his eighteen years, and remained friends with every single one of them. But right now he’s hoping to hold on to his current girlfriend, the gloriously fat and beautiful Cassidy – of Icelandic eyes and Nordic locks. But Sutter can’t do the one thing that Cassidy asks of him; to consider her feelings. So Cassidy dumps him, and Sutter finds healing in the bottom of a whisky bottle. . . <br /><br />Aimee Finicky finds Sutter passed out on a strangers’ lawn. Of course she knows who he is, they’ve been going to the same school for years now and she can remember every class they shared and every hilarious thing he did – he’s cool and popular, so it’s no wonder he doesn’t recognise quiet, shy Aimee. <br /><br />After sharing a paper-route one morning, Sutter decides to ‘save’ Aimee. She has no self-esteem, a gambling mother and Walrus-like stepfather. She wears a purple puffer jacket that makes her look like a Christmas ornament, and her best friend is a miniature tyrant. Sutter decides to take her under his wing, and not a moment too soon. <br /><br />But it might not be Aimee who’s in desperate need of help. After all, Sutter has never quite recovered from his parent’s divorce and lies to himself about his idyllic absentee father. His sister has been angry with him ever since he set her husband’s suit on fire. And his best friend, Ricky, has gained a girlfriend and some perspective on Sutter’s wild partying ways. Then, of course, there’s Cassidy – who Sutter stills pines for, and intends to win back. <br /><br />Sutter Keely may be the life of every party, but at some point the lights always come on and the music eventually fades. <br /><br />‘The Spectacular Now’ is the 2008 young adult novel by Tim Tharp, which was a National Book Award Finalist.<br /><br />I've been recommended this book for a solid five years now. I bought it and added to the TBR pile, and would occasionally re-read the blurb or scan the first page – but I was never moved to read. And then I heard from Persnickety Snark that a film adaptation was screening to rave reviews at Sundance Film Festival. This intrigued me. And when I found out Shailene Woodley (‘The Descendants’) was in the lead as Aimee, I decided to get on board this bandwagon. And I’m sooooooo glad I did, because ‘The Spectacular Now’ is flippin’ superb, and if it's half as good a movie as it is a book, then it will live up to the spectacular. <br /><br />There’s a certain plot trope called ‘Beautiful All Along’ – which is as it sounds, that a nerdy-type girl is plucked out of social obscurity by the popular jock who then makes her over, only to discover she was Beautiful All Along. Weeeeeeell . . . Tim Tharp takes that trope, puts it into a blender and hits ‘obliterate’, and what pours out is a disarmingly complex and refreshing young adult novel that’s part comedy with a heavy dose of stalled morality. <br /><br />Our ‘jock’ in this case is no jock, but rather popular party boy Sutter Keely who doesn’t think he’s an alcoholic, even though he frequently drinks first thing in the morning and by himself. He’s a good, harmless guy but he’s vapid and seriously lacking in self-awareness. Aimee is no nerd, but rather a downtrodden wallflower with the world on her shoulders. And rather than the Beautiful All Along story being told from Aimee’s perspective, we get it from Sutter’s. This is not a romance – and that will frustrate some people. Sutter is not a knight in shining armour – he’s a ticking time bomb who doesn’t know he is his own detonator and Aimee is his doomed damsel. <br /><br />Tharp has such a great rhythm in this book. Sutter is a genuinely funny guy, he’s charismatic and oozing a certain <i>je ne sais quoi</i> that makes him utterly endearing. But slowly Tharp starts chipping away at Sutter’s armour to reveal the crippling lies he tells himself – and readers start to see what a few of his classmates have already realized; that Sutter believes those lies.<br /><br />While I was reading this I was thinking that it would be a hard book to adapt, only because the writing is so lush and Sutter’s interior voice so vital to the book. Tharp writes something delicious. It’s little things in the description; <br /><br /><i>Her voice is so soft. If it were a food item, it’d be a marshmallow. </i><br /><br />But Sutter’s worldview monologues are also kinda brilliant, and I'd hate to lose them in the screenplay. So I was really happy to see one movie review in particular that says there are long stretches of banter and blocks of back-and-forth dialogue between characters. <br /><br /><i>We’re not the Faster-than-the-Speed-of-Light Generation anymore. We’re not even the Next-New-Thing Generation. We’re the Soon-to-Be-Obsolete Kids, and we’ve crowded in here to hide from the future and the past. We know what’s up – the future looms straight ahead like a black wrought-iron gate and the past is charging after us like a badass Doberman, only this one doesn’t have any letup in him. </i><br /><br />Now, as to the Sutter and Aimee ‘romance’ – some people will hate it. They’ll just downright hate it. But I revelled in its originality and honesty; I was so glad that Tharp took the road less travelled in teen romances, and the book is the better for it. <br /><br /><i>“Hey, I told you – I’m not going to ask her out for a date. Let me repeat, she is not a girl I’m interested in having sex with. Not now or any time in the future. I will not have sex with her in a car. I will not have sex with her in a bar. I will not have sex with her in a tree. I will not have sex with her in a lavatory-ee. I will not have sex with her in a chair. I will not have sex with her anywhere.”<br />“Oh right, I forgot. You’re out to save her soul. Give me a hallelujah for Brother Sutter and his messianic complex.”<br />“My what?”<br />“Messianic complex. That means you think you have to go around trying to save everybody.”<br />“Not everybody. Just this one girl.”<br />“Hallelujah, brother!”</i><br /><br />Look, this book will kick your ass a little bit. There’s this weird thing that happens where, as a reader, you become sort of like Sutter’s girlfriends; all those who fell for his rambunctious charm and carefree loving-life in the beginning, but slowly figured out his failings and shortcomings, becoming frustrated with his wasted potential. The ending is brutal perfection, and if Tharp had concluded any other way, then the entire book would have been a sell-out. As it is, ‘The Spectacular Now’ is one of the cleverest and truest YA books I've ever read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="22331481160965451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2483935711" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604273386p2/64621419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483935711?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375865022" href="/book/show/7961827-the-spectacular-now">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483935711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3426109303385778569">Didn't turn out the way I hoped it would. And after some pondering I think I actually like it for that exact reason.<br/><br/>It's the story of a high schooler that's partying a lot, drinking way too much and seemingly can't hold on to any relationships with girls. Because at some point being fun and all isn't enough. You have to have some direction in which your life is going. And Sutter just doesn't. He lives in the spectacular now. <br/><br/>The main character is simultaneously loveable and an ass. He definitely</span>
  <span id="freeText3426109303385778569" style="display:none">Didn't turn out the way I hoped it would. And after some pondering I think I actually like it for that exact reason.<br /><br />It's the story of a high schooler that's partying a lot, drinking way too much and seemingly can't hold on to any relationships with girls. Because at some point being fun and all isn't enough. You have to have some direction in which your life is going. And Sutter just doesn't. He lives in the spectacular now. <br /><br />The main character is simultaneously loveable and an ass. He definitely has some serious problems and unappealing traits. But he's also got heart. He's not a role model and I really hope teenagers reading this book realize that. But I still liked him.<br /><br />At one point Aimee steps into his life. She's that nerdy and shy and good-natured and just really sweet girl. You only wish the best for her. And you think she just might be what Sutter needs and you hope he doesn't hurt her.<br /><br />And then everything was going in a different direction from what I expected. <br /><br />The book feels very real. Sometimes too real. Because me having to "listen" to Sutter talking like, well, a teenager got on my nerves quite a bit on several occasions. I might be getting a little too old for YA. Or maybe not. There's still hope.<br /><br />Anyhow, the few annoying bits notwithstanding, this one was funny and sad and even deep sometimes and entertaining all the way through. And just when I was starting to get annoyed about the direction it took I realized I was wrong. After all, I really liked the ending and finally was able to appreciate what the author was doing here.<br /><br />Now I have to re-watch the movie, because even though I know I liked it, I clearly couldn't remember the details very well.<br />Good thing we've got that one lined up already. :)<br /><br /><br /><i>So, we've seen the movie last night and I have to say I didn't like it as much as the first time around.<br /><br />It stays close to the source material for most of its 95 minute running time. But it's just too short. Some events are left out, of course. And that's really inevitable and was okay. But the two main characters suffer the most from the short running time. They're just not that well developed in the film.<br /><br />Even though the casting of Miles Teller as Sutter and Shailene Woodley as Aimee was just perfect, they both got shortchanged by the script.<br /><br />I'm not denying that the movie had emotional impact, especially towards the end. But the characters' motivations became a lot clearer in the book. And even though that's almost always the case, there's a rather vast disparity here.<br /><br />I also liked it better how the book ended in comparison to the movie. Don't know why they changed it.<br /><br />Oh well, I still liked it. But the book ruined it a little for me.<br /><br /><b>The book: 4/5</b><br />The movie: 6.5/10</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3426109303385778569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="Heidi " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi " href="/user/show/416888-heidi">Heidi </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2054282676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8246825619529925417">Moments of my own high school experience flashed through my mind as I read this. It's like going back and glimpsing what's really going on in the mind of the class clown or partier. Funny, sad, pathetic, sympathetic... and most importantly, pretty darn authentic. <br/><br/>Addiction, no matter the age, is complicated... as is young love and figuring it all out before the weight of your future crashes down. <br/><br/>Interesting ending... maybe more authenticity than the reader bargains for... but isn't that just li</span>
  <span id="freeText8246825619529925417" style="display:none">Moments of my own high school experience flashed through my mind as I read this. It's like going back and glimpsing what's really going on in the mind of the class clown or partier. Funny, sad, pathetic, sympathetic... and most importantly, pretty darn authentic. <br /><br />Addiction, no matter the age, is complicated... as is young love and figuring it all out before the weight of your future crashes down. <br /><br />Interesting ending... maybe more authenticity than the reader bargains for... but isn't that just like real life?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8246825619529925417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
