<div id="review_511280232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/511280232" />
    <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard"><img alt="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321462468p2/2216677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/511280232?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard">Cassi aka Snow White Haggard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423399636" href="/book/show/7961828-spectacular-now-the">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer511280232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7928617375414271240">The Spectacular Now is a strange sort of book. I want to lecture it, to give it my own personal big-sister talking to. In some ways I wanted to hate it because the way it almost glorified teenage drinking and partying.<br/><br/>But I can't. Because even if I don't agree with Sutter's methods, he feels like a real believable teenager. Sometimes it's brave for a book to portray drinking (I would call Sutter a teenage alcoholic but I don't think he would) without ever getting preachy or putting on the parent</span>
  <span id="freeText7928617375414271240" style="display:none">The Spectacular Now is a strange sort of book. I want to lecture it, to give it my own personal big-sister talking to. In some ways I wanted to hate it because the way it almost glorified teenage drinking and partying.<br /><br />But I can't. Because even if I don't agree with Sutter's methods, he feels like a real believable teenager. Sometimes it's brave for a book to portray drinking (I would call Sutter a teenage alcoholic but I don't think he would) without ever getting preachy or putting on the parent hat. It's disarming, but sometimes it's good for a book to rile us up and challenge what we think is right.<br /><br />Sutter is one of those kids, the party boy with a heart of gold. To some people this might seem unrealistic, but it's not. I never knew a guy quite like Sutter, but I had a friend who was in and out of trouble in high school. For a goody-two-shoes like me, knowing him was a bit of a revelation. Yes he had problems, illegal ones, but he was a really good friend to me. Sometime's it's easy to label someone as a "bad guy" but it's much more realistic and complicated to acknowledge that sometimes there are good people with good hearts who still do bad things.<br /><br />Sutter is like that. Yes he's probably an alcoholic, but he's trying to be a good friend and he really does genuinely cares about people. He just doesn't believe he can be anything more than the party guy. Beneath the fun party-loving facade, Sutter's real problem is that he doesn't think he's worthy of being loved. He always thinks everyone is going to leave him. So rather than tackle that head on, he drinks and keeps people at arm's length.<br /><br />This story is not a lifetime-original movie, where a teenage alcoholic finds redemption. It's a story where Sutter accidentally learns to love and learns to be loved. This book is full of imperfect people who are just trying to figure out how to live life, have fun and be happy without bulldozing over everybody around them.<br /><br />This book is a rarity. It made me angry, made me think and made me cry. In some ways it feels like a very dangerous books, that a teenager could walk away with entirely the wrong message, but I don't think every YA book needs to preach a sermon. The Spectacular Now tells a good story with believable imperfect characters. People are complicated and messy -- good, bad, stupid, careless, all of the above. But that doesn't mean they aren't valuable and don't contribute something to the world. That's the heart of this book.<br /><br />Note:I listened to the audiobook and the narration is superb.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7928617375414271240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18427857300769930363"><b>My Actual Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>The Spectacular Now is just so genuine that it hurts. It just hurts in the worst possible way ever. <br/><br/>What shattered me the most was the book's ending. Did it really have to end like that? As much as I want more and even if it tore me to pieces and left me wanting so much more - for Sutter to get better, for him to finally change - I think, yes. Because knowing that if these things happen it will just wash away the realness of this book. That's what life is. It's a mess.</span>
  <span id="freeText18427857300769930363" style="display:none"><b>My Actual Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br /><br />The Spectacular Now is just so genuine that it hurts. It just hurts in the worst possible way ever. <br /><br />What shattered me the most was the book's ending. Did it really have to end like that? As much as I want more and even if it tore me to pieces and left me wanting so much more - for Sutter to get better, for him to finally change - I think, yes. Because knowing that if these things happen it will just wash away the realness of this book. That's what life is. It's a mess. And no mess can ever be solved if we don't do anything about it. Sutter, he just remained living in his spectacular now. He thought he could save someone but he never once thought that maybe he was the one in need of saving. But maybe not everybody could ever be saved. I guess that's what Tim Tharp's trying to tell us all.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_650109446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650109446" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/650109446?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8339396-the-spectacular-now">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=book-to-film-or-tv">book-to-film-or-tv</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650109446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11023506346407621724">My rating: 2 of 5 stars<br/>Source: Library Checkout<br/><br/><i>'Another spectacular afternoon. This weather is unbelievable. Of course, that probably means summer is going to be vicious again, but I'm not worried about that now. I was never big on the future. I admire people who are, but it just never was my thing.'</i><br/><br/>Sutter is spontaneous with a luring personality who lives life solely in the moment. Aimee is plagued by insecurity but has a mind that is saturated with dreams of the future. The two are an unlikely</span>
  <span id="freeText11023506346407621724" style="display:none">My rating: 2 of 5 stars<br />Source: Library Checkout<br /><br /><i>'Another spectacular afternoon. This weather is unbelievable. Of course, that probably means summer is going to be vicious again, but I'm not worried about that now. I was never big on the future. I admire people who are, but it just never was my thing.'</i><br /><br />Sutter is spontaneous with a luring personality who lives life solely in the moment. Aimee is plagued by insecurity but has a mind that is saturated with dreams of the future. The two are an unlikely combination but Aimee is mesmerized by the lifestyle Sutter leads and Sutter is convinced he can do Aimee good by giving her the confidence she needs so badly.<br /><br /><i>'To hell with tomorrow. To hell with all problems and barriers. Nothing matters but the Spectacular Now.'</i><br /><br />Oh, Sutter. His character is not portrayed solely as an addict or an alcoholic, instead he's this extremely fun and charismatic person that everyone really can't help but love... he just has a serious problem with alcohol. But that's not his defining feature. There was a complete lack of character development in regards to Sutter; he simply maintained as he was first introduced. I definitely wished I had seen some alteration, even slight, especially since this is highly considered to be a coming of age tale and I require character development in order for that label to be fitting.<br /><br />Considering this story is told from the point of view of Sutter, everything is glorified because that's the mentality he projects on the world. Unfortunately, the same goes for his alcoholic tendencies. It's reflected in such a glamorized and non-gritty light and I can't help but take issue with that since this book is targeted towards children. Taken at face value I think it would be difficult for children to see past the facade and realize that Sutter has a serious issue. The ending sheds some light on the seriousness but not enough in my opinion. Sutter's story is truly a tragedy, I can only hope that for those children that do read this have parents that are willing to sit down and discuss with them the ravaging effects of alcohol. <br /><br />Despite his good intentions towards Aimee, their relationship is truly toxic. The effect Sutter had on her was initially beneficial, however, she ended up turning down the exact road as him as her grades began to slip and she began drinking (almost) as much as him. What astonished me most was the family members of both main characters and their complete absence in their lives. I understand being a parent myself and not being able to see issues all the time before they rear their ugly head but Sutter made the fact that he was on a downward spiral loud and clear. <br /><br />My opinion is quite the unpopular one regarding this book. This was well written and an honest depiction of alcoholism, I just didn't agree with the glamorized feel the book lent it, especially when you consider the target audience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11023506346407621724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_305513491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305513491" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305513491?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305513491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13647102836334193759">I'd have never picked up this novel in a million years if it weren't for the fact that the screen writers of "500 Days of Summer" wrote the screenplay for the movie version of this novel. And Shailene Woodley, of course. It seems a little shallow to admit that, but it's the truth. I'm not a fan of Contemporary YA and I'm especially not a fan of novels about teenagers partying and drinking - which is, admittedly, a lot of what this book is. <br/><br/>Yet, the narration throughout this story is superb. Sutt</span>
  <span id="freeText13647102836334193759" style="display:none">I'd have never picked up this novel in a million years if it weren't for the fact that the screen writers of "500 Days of Summer" wrote the screenplay for the movie version of this novel. And Shailene Woodley, of course. It seems a little shallow to admit that, but it's the truth. I'm not a fan of Contemporary YA and I'm especially not a fan of novels about teenagers partying and drinking - which is, admittedly, a lot of what this book is. <br /><br />Yet, the narration throughout this story is superb. Sutter, the teen who has popularity, a car, a job, and a girlfriend. A really big heart. But also a drinking problem. An addiction. And reading his tale is a little like stepping into that mindset yourself. It captures the essence of the teenage years, but also the scary cliff that looms ahead when you're lost in your world. Sutter is so deeply dark with so many layers to just keep peeling. Aimee, the girl he intends to save, is just as screwed up in some ways and I love her unrelenting depths as well. All of these characters are written so starkly; realistic and raw in a manner that is difficult to describe. And this ending, though not the one I was clamoring for, did manage to grasp life in all its highs and lows. THE SPECTACULAR NOW is a spectacular slice of life itself, with all its messiness and flaws, complications and oddities, and though it's not my favorite book out there, I can't recommend it enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13647102836334193759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1272650917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1272650917" />
    <a title="Halle Watson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23644667-halle-watson"><img alt="Halle Watson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606109484p2/23644667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1272650917?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Halle Watson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Halle Watson" href="/user/show/23644667-halle-watson">Halle Watson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23644667-halle-watson?shelf=so-many-feels">so-many-feels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272650917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4820716184573214040"><b>We all know Sutter Keely.</b> Maybe we don’t want to know him. Maybe we are ashamed that we knew him. Maybe we jumped on his bandwagon for a short time in high school, but we likely knew him in one form or another.<br/><br/>He is the life of the party; the one who is okay with destroying people's houses when he parties. The kid that you know has alcohol in the back of his car and can’t seem to knock any sense into himself. He is drunk before, during, and after school (if he doesn’t skip) and is set on enjoyin</span>
  <span id="freeText4820716184573214040" style="display:none"><b>We all know Sutter Keely.</b> Maybe we don’t want to know him. Maybe we are ashamed that we knew him. Maybe we jumped on his bandwagon for a short time in high school, but we likely knew him in one form or another.<br><br>He is the life of the party; the one who is okay with destroying people's houses when he parties. The kid that you know has alcohol in the back of his car and can’t seem to knock any sense into himself. He is drunk before, during, and after school (if he doesn’t skip) and is set on enjoying the present, and avoiding the future. He is obsessed with “the spectacular now.”<br><br>But for him, it isn’t very spectacular.<br><br><b>I loved this book in spite of Sutter.</b> He wasn’t an enjoyable character and I kept thinking, “I know people just like you. Don’t throw your life away like them!” But he just wasn’t listening to me (or maybe he was too drunk to care). But he was real. Real frustrating. Real annoying. Real reckless, but he was real.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431620202ra/14854295.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No, Aimee. He is not okay. He is a terrible mess who can't seem to realize he is a mess. <br><br>Ricky and Aimee were my favorite characters because they both reacted so differently to Sutter’s lifestyle. Aimee enabled him because she craved love and affection while Ricky enjoyed it until it was time to grow up and think about the future.<br><br>Sutter takes Aimee on as a project to show her exactly how spectacular now can be, but he started to ruin Aimee with his lifestyle. She was innocent and kind, but let everyone else walk all over her. He may have taught her how to stand up to her friends and her parents, but never showed her how to stand up to him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431620202ra/14854296.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431620202ra/14854297.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Cute, right?</b> Well it's only cute until he starts to ruin her life in a different way than everyone else did.<br><br>The realism in this book was like a slap in the face. Not every story is a gushy romance or a story of redemption. Some stories are just about people never get over their problems and only manage to drag others down with them.<br><br>I almost gave this book four stars, but I realized that was <b>so</b> stupid of me. I wanted to take a star from the author because I didn’t like the way it ended, when it was far more likely to end that way all along.<br><br>Maybe I didn’t get the ending I wanted, but these characters got the ending they deserved.<br><br><br>This can also be found on my blog <a href="http://www.bighairbiggerbooks.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Hair Bigger Books</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4820716184573214040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1025700059" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025700059" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3600343-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332418902p2/3600343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025700059?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/3600343-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3600343-rob?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025700059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18349085003806097860">There's that old literary saw that says if the main character of a book doesn't change, the book is a failure. But what if the unchanging main character is the catalyst by which others are allowed to change? That's the fascinating issue at the heart of <i>The Spectacular Now,</i> a book whose protagonist is a drunken – but charismatically drunken – high school senior named Sutter Keely. He's the life of the party, a barely-functioning teenage alcoholic who's so filled with love for his fellow man that </span>
  <span id="freeText18349085003806097860" style="display:none">There's that old literary saw that says if the main character of a book doesn't change, the book is a failure. But what if the unchanging main character is the catalyst by which others are allowed to change? That's the fascinating issue at the heart of <i>The Spectacular Now,</i> a book whose protagonist is a drunken – but charismatically drunken – high school senior named Sutter Keely. He's the life of the party, a barely-functioning teenage alcoholic who's so filled with love for his fellow man that he views his drinking as a way to bring joy to others.<br /><br />It's this perceived selflessness that leads him to woo Aimee Finecky, a shy, awkward bookworm (she's big into science-fiction) who becomes, at least at first, his pet project. He initially goes out with her as a way of giving her self-confidence so that one day she might actually have a chance with a "real" boyfriend. At least that's what he tells himself. But even though Sutter goes out of his way to point out that Aimee isn't conventionally beautiful or the type he usually goes for, it's clear that he's falling for her (and she for him), and this pet project slowly turns into something real.<br /><br />And of course this scares him, because deep at Sutter's core is a fear of abandonment that grows out of his father's desertion when he was young. This makes Sutter a spectacularly complex character – one who believes strongly in the value of others but saves none of it for himself. There's a compelling push/pull at the center of his relationship with Aimee as he continually pushes her to be a better person while continually sabotaging himself. The book ends in a dark place for Sutter, a place where all we can do is hope that things eventually turn around for, as he calls himself, God's own drunk.<br /><br />A quick note for people who saw and loved the movie (as I did). The book is even better, partly because as narrator Sutter's motivations are much clearer, but also because Aimee is obviously <i>not</i> a Shailene Woodley type. Woodley is terrific in the movie and plays awkward so well, but she's such a strong personality that it was hard to buy her as a teen with no friends and no confidence. In the book, however, Aimee's transformation is much more pronounced precisely because author Tim Tharp draws her as such a beaten-down character. The movie and the book are both fantastic, but for very different reasons.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18349085003806097860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_56189532" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56189532" />
    <a title="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/289556-jackie-the-librarian"><img alt="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307387831p2/289556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56189532?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" href="/user/show/289556-jackie-the-librarian">Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56189532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15664698318872278366">Sutter Keely is a lot of fun. The life of the party! All his girlfriends have the greatest time with him. So, why do they all break up with him? Don't they LIKE having fun? So, he enjoys drinking - what's wrong with that? It's not like he's a <i>mean</i> drunk, at all.<br/> <br/>As a reader, I felt like one of Sutter's girlfriends. At first, yeah, it <i>was</i> fun, if a little appalling, to read about Sutter's drunken adventures, giving a runaway kid a ride home while skipping school himself, meeting a shy newspaper d</span>
  <span id="freeText15664698318872278366" style="display:none">Sutter Keely is a lot of fun. The life of the party! All his girlfriends have the greatest time with him. So, why do they all break up with him? Don't they LIKE having fun? So, he enjoys drinking - what's wrong with that? It's not like he's a <i>mean</i> drunk, at all.<br /> <br />As a reader, I felt like one of Sutter's girlfriends. At first, yeah, it <i>was</i> fun, if a little appalling, to read about Sutter's drunken adventures, giving a runaway kid a ride home while skipping school himself, meeting a shy newspaper delivery girl and bringing some fun into her life. He <i>is</i> a nice guy, you think. Maybe Aimee, the nerdy but cute newspaper girl, can help turn him around.<br /><br />But then, when Sutter won't acknowledge Aimee's growing attraction to him, or the fact that he's turning her into a drunk, too, then loses his job because he keeps coming in buzzed, and we learn the truth about his father, we begin to see Sutter in a new light. And it's not pretty. <br /><br />By the end of the book, I, like all of Sutter's girlfriends, was ready to kick him to the curb, and tell him to grow up. Drinking all the time, not cool, man. Letting your grades slide, and never being trustworthy, really just not cool. Hopefully, teens who read this will feel the same way, and not just think Sutter's cool. Because he's not. He's pathetic. And this book is masterful at revealing this in a way that isn't didactic or message-y, but just lets Sutter's own behavior speak for itself. <br /><br />Recommended for older teens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15664698318872278366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F29Ht2ME3hG2STUUMMRFXKP2VQxtst5zhA7EPMp4X834lXaePf6ShdhUQ/ctkX9tfB3HBWOAUpEkx2xOphS/lA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YACLhvomWN7Z2I3x9kMccazZCDn2dg7xBYGA5pqp4IGP+rqvpNwUSrfF+xLrFiZAczKaMPhEghOlSCiU9sUA2A==')})
  }

Written with an immediate sense of place--claustrophobic and ominous--James Franco\'s collection traces the lives of an extended group of teenagers as they experiment with vices of all kinds, struggle with their families and one another, and succumb to self-destructive, often heartless nihilism. In &quot;Lockheed&quot; a young woman\'s summer--spent working a dull internship--is suddenly upended by a spectacular incident of violence at a house party.  In &quot;American History&quot; a high school freshman attempts to impress a girl during a classroom skit with a realistic portrayal of a slave owner—only to have his feigned bigotry avenged. In &quot;I Could Kill Someone,&quot; a lonely teenager buys a gun with the aim of killing his high school tormentor, but begins to wonder about his bully\'s own inner life. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6062171773359294678">Tim Tharp lives in Oklahoma where he writes novels and teaches in the Humanities Department at Rose State College. In addition to earning a B.A. from the University of Oklahoma and an M.F.A. from Brown University, Tim Tharp has been a factory hand, construction laborer, psychiatric aid, long-distance hitchhiker, and record store clerk. His first novel, Falling Dark (Milkweed Press), was awarded th</span>
  <span id="freeText6062171773359294678" style="display:none">Tim Tharp lives in Oklahoma where he writes novels and teaches in the Humanities Department at Rose State College. In addition to earning a B.A. from the University of Oklahoma and an M.F.A. from Brown University, Tim Tharp has been a factory hand, construction laborer, psychiatric aid, long-distance hitchhiker, and record store clerk. His first novel, Falling Dark (Milkweed Press), was awarded the Milkweed National Fiction Prize. Knights of the Hill Country (Knopf Books for Young Readers) is his first novel for young adults and was named to the American Library Association's Best Books of 2007 list. Tim's new YA novel, The Spectacular Now, (Knopf Books, Nov. 2008) was a finalist for the 2008 National Book Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6062171773359294678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
